</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-constant)\">9.9999</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">.</span></li></ol></pre>\n<p><i id=\"p_203\" class=\"pid\"></i>Except now, behind the scenes, and without any changes to the frontend, Alice takes two steps in our program and Bob only takes one, and she is protected against Bob finding her hand and using it to ensure he wins!<a href=\"#p_203\" class=\"pid\">203</a></p>\n<p>\n  <i id=\"p_204\" class=\"pid\"></i>When we compile this version of the application, Reach's <a href=\"/guide/assert/#guide-assert\">automatic formal verification</a> engine proves many theorems and protects us against a plethora of mistakes one might make when writing even a simple application like this.\n  Non-Reach programmers that try to write decentralized applications are on their own trying to ensure that these problems don't exist.<a href=\"#p_204\" class=\"pid\">204</a>\n</p>\n<div class=\"note\">\n  <p><i id=\"p_205\" class=\"pid\"></i>If your version isn't working, look at the complete versions of <a href=\"https://github.com/reach-sh/reach-lang/tree/master/examples/rps-5-trust/index.rsh\"><code>rps-5-trust/index.rsh</code></a> and <a href=\"https://github.com/reach-sh/reach-lang/tree/master/examples/rps-5-trust/index.mjs\"><code>rps-5-trust/index.mjs</code></a> to make sure you copied everything down correctly!<a href=\"#p_205\" class=\"pid\">205</a></p>\n</div>\n<p>\n  <i id=\"p_206\" class=\"pid\"></i>Now our implementation of <em>Rock, Paper, Scissors!</em> is secure and doesn't contain any exploits for either Alice or Bob to guarantee a win.\n  However, it still has a final category of mistake that is common in decentralized applications: <a href=\"/guide/timeout/#guide-timeout\">non-participation</a>.\n  We'll fix this in <a href=\"/tut/rps/#tut-6\">the next step</a>; make sure you don't launch with this version, or Alice may decide to back out of the game when she knows she's going to lose!<a href=\"#p_206\" class=\"pid\">206</a>\n</p>\n<div class=\"q-and-a\" data-bs-toggle=\"collapse\" aria-expanded=\"false\" href=\"#q4\">\n  <p><i id=\"p_207\" class=\"pid\"></i>Since blockchain programs run on a single, global, publicly-checked and certified consensus network, you dont need to test them as much as normal software, which run on a wide variety of different platforms and operating systems.<a href=\"#p_207\" class=\"pid\">207</a></p>\n  <div class=\"collapse\" id=\"q4\">\n    <p><i id=\"p_208\" class=\"pid\"></i>False<a href=\"#p_208\" class=\"pid\">208</a></p>\n  </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"q-and-a\" data-bs-toggle=\"collapse\" aria-expanded=\"false\" href=\"#q5\">\n  <p><i id=\"p_209\" class=\"pid\"></i>It is easy to write correct programs that handle financial information, and even if you make a mistake, blockchains support an \"Undo\" operation that allows you to rollback to earlier versions of the ledger to correct mistakes and recover lost funds.<a href=\"#p_209\" class=\"pid\">209</a></p>\n  <div class=\"collapse\" id=\"q5\">\n    <p><i id=\"p_210\" class=\"pid\"></i>False<a href=\"#p_210\" class=\"pid\">210</a></p>\n  </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"q-and-a\" data-bs-toggle=\"collapse\" aria-expanded=\"false\" href=\"#q6\">\n  <p><i id=\"p_211\" class=\"pid\"></i>Reach provides automatic verifications to ensure that your program does not lose, lock away, or overspend funds and guarantees that your applications are free from entire categories of errors.<a href=\"#p_211\" class=\"pid\">211</a></p>\n  <div class=\"collapse\" id=\"q6\">\n    <p><i id=\"p_212\" class=\"pid\"></i>True<a href=\"#p_212\" class=\"pid\">212</a></p>\n  </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"q-and-a\" data-bs-toggle=\"collapse\" aria-expanded=\"false\" href=\"#q7\">\n  <p><i id=\"p_213\" class=\"pid\"></i>Reach provides tools for you to add custom verifications to your program, like ensuring that information is known only to one party, or that your implementation of a sensitive algorithm is correct.<a href=\"#p_213\" class=\"pid\">213</a></p>\n  <div class=\"collapse\" id=\"q7\">\n    <p><i id=\"p_214\" class=\"pid\"></i>True<a href=\"#p_214\" class=\"pid\">214</a></p>\n  </div>\n</div>\n<h2 id=\"tut-6\" class=\"refHeader\">Timeouts and Participation<a aria-hidden=\"true\" tabindex=\"-1\" href=\"#tut-6\"><span class=\"icon icon-link\"></span></a></h2>\n<p>\n  <i id=\"p_215\" class=\"pid\"></i>In the last section, we removed a security vulnerability from <em>Rock, Paper, Scissors!</em> that was a clear attack on the viability of the application.\n  In this section, we'll focus on a more subtle issue that is important and unique to decentralized applications: <a href=\"/guide/timeout/#guide-timeout\">non-participation</a>.<a href=\"#p_215\" class=\"pid\">215</a>\n</p>\n<p><i id=\"p_216\" class=\"pid\"></i>Non-participation refers to the act of one party ceasing to continue playing their role in an application.<a href=\"#p_216\" class=\"pid\">216</a></p>\n<p>\n  <i id=\"p_217\" class=\"pid\"></i>In traditional client-server programs, like a Web server, this would be the case of a client not sending any more requests to the server, or the server stopping sending responses to the client.\n  In these sorts of traditional programs, non-participation is an exceptional circumstance that normally leads to an error message for clients and, at most, a log entry for servers.\n  Sometimes traditional programs will need to recycle resources, like network ports, on non-participation, but they would have also needed to do that if the transaction ended by normal means.\n  In other words, for traditional client-server programs, it is not necessary for designers to meticulously consider the consequences of non-participation.<a href=\"#p_217\" class=\"pid\">217</a>\n</p>\n<p>\n  <i id=\"p_218\" class=\"pid\"></i>In contrast, decentralized applications must be carefully designed with an eye towards their behavior in the face of non-participation.\n  For example, consider what happens in our <em>Rock, Paper, Scissors!</em> game if after Alice has paid her wager, Bob never accepts and the application doesn't continue.\n  In this case, Alice's network tokens would be locked inside of the contract and lost to her.\n  Similarly, if after Bob accepted and paid his wager, Alice stopped participating and never submitted her hand, then both their funds would be locked away forever.\n  In each of these cases, both parties would be greatly hurt and their fear of that outcome would introduce an additional cost to transacting, which would lower the value they got from participating in the application.\n  Of course, in a situation like <em>Rock, Paper, Scissors!</em> this is unlikely to be an important matter, but recall that <em>Rock, Paper, Scissors!</em> is a microcosm of decentralized application design.<a href=\"#p_218\" class=\"pid\">218</a>\n</p>\n<div class=\"note\">\n  <p>\n    <i id=\"p_219\" class=\"pid\"></i>Technically, in the first case, when Bob fails to start the application, Alice is not locked away from her funds: since Bob's identity is not fixed until after his first message, she could start another instance of the game as the Bob role and then she'd win all of the funds, less any transaction costs of the consensus network.\n    In the second case, however, there would be no recourse for either party.<a href=\"#p_219\" class=\"pid\">219</a>\n  </p>\n</div>\n<p>\n  <i id=\"p_220\" class=\"pid\"></i>In the rest of this section, we'll discuss how Reach helps address non-participation.\n  For a longer discussion, refer to <a href=\"/guide/timeout/#guide-timeout\">the guide chapter on non-participation</a>.<a href=\"#p_220\" class=\"pid\">220</a>\n</p>\n<hr>\n<p>\n  <i id=\"p_221\" class=\"pid\"></i>In Reach, non-participation is handled through a \"timeout\" mechanism whereby each consensus transfer can be paired with a step that occurs for all participants if the originator of the consensus transfer fails to make the required publication before a particular network time.\n  We'll integrate this mechanism into our version of <em>Rock, Paper, Scissors!</em> and deliberately insert non-participation into our JavaScript testing program to watch the consequences play out.<a href=\"#p_221\" class=\"pid\">221</a>\n</p>\n<p><i id=\"p_222\" class=\"pid\"></i>First, we'll modify the participant interact interface to allow the frontend to be informed that a timeout occurred.<a href=\"#p_222\" class=\"pid\">222</a></p>\n<pre class=\"snippet numbered\"><div class=\"codeHeader\"><a href=\"https://github.com/reach-sh/reach-lang/tree/master/examples/rps-6-timeouts/index.rsh\">/examples/rps-6-timeouts/index.rsh</a><a class=\"far fa-copy copyBtn\" data-clipboard-text=\"const Player = {\n  ...hasRandom,\n  getHand: Fun([], UInt),\n  seeOutcome: Fun([UInt], Null),\n  informTimeout: Fun([], Null),\n};\" href=\"#\"></a></div><ol class=\"snippet\"><li value=\"20\"><a var(--shiki-token-constant)\">Player</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\"> </span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-keyword)\">=</span><span style=\"color: value=\"22\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">  getHand</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-keyword)\">:</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\"> </span><a href=\"/rsh/compute/#rsh_Fun\" title=\"rsh: Fun\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-function)\">Fun</span></a><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">([]</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-punctuation)\">,</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\"> UInt)</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-punctuation)\">,</span></li><li value=\"23\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">  seeOutcome</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-keyword)\">:</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\"> </span><a href=\"/rsh/compute/#rsh_Fun\" title=\"rsh: Fun\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-function)\">Fun</span></a><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">([UInt]</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-punctuation)\">,</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\"> Null)</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-punctuation)\">,</span></li><li value=\"24\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">  informTimeout</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-keyword)\">:</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\"> </span><a href=\"/rsh/compute/#rsh_Fun\" title=\"rsh: Fun\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-function)\">Fun</span></a><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">([]</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-punctuation)\">,</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\"> Null)</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-punctuation)\">,</span></li><li value=\"25\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">};</span></li></ol></pre>\n<ul>\n  <li>\n    <i id=\"p_223\" class=\"pid\"></i>Line 24 introduces a new method, <span class=\"snip\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">informTimeout</span></span>, that receives no arguments and returns no information.\n    We'll call this function when a timeout occurs.<a href=\"#p_223\" class=\"pid\">223</a>\n  </li>\n</ul>\n<p><i id=\"p_224\" class=\"pid\"></i>We'll make a slight tweak to our JavaScript frontend to be able to receive this message and display it on the console.<a href=\"#p_224\" class=\"pid\">224</a></p>\n<pre class=\"snippet numbered\"><div class=\"codeHeader\"><a href=\"https://github.com/reach-sh/reach-lang/tree/master/examples/rps-6-timeouts/index.mjs\">/examples/rps-6-timeouts/index.mjs</a><a class=\"far fa-copy copyBtn\" data-clipboard-text=\"const Player = (Who) => ({\n  ...stdlib.hasRandom,\n  getHand: () => {\n    const hand = Math.floor(Math.random() * 3);\n    console.log(`${Who} played ${HAND[hand]}`);\n    return hand;\n  },\n  seeOutcome: style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">  </span><a href=\"/rsh/consensus/#rsh_commit\" title=\"rsh: commit\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-function)\">commit</span></a><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">();</span></li></ol></pre>\n<ul>\n  <li><i id=\"p_236\" class=\"pid\"></i>Line 63 adds a timeout handler to Bob's publication.<a href=\"#p_236\" class=\"pid\">236</a></li>\n</ul>\n<p>\n  <i id=\"p_237\" class=\"pid\"></i>The timeout handler specifies that if Bob does not complete this action within a time delta of <span class=\"snip\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">deadline</span></span>, then the application transitions to the step given by the arrow expression.\n  In this case, the timeout code is a call to <span class=\"snip\"><a href=\"/rsh/step/#rsh_closeTo\" title=\"rsh: closeTo\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">closeTo</span></a></span>, which is a Reach standard library function that allows anyone to send a message and transfer all of the funds in the contract to Alice, then call the given function afterwards.\n  This means that if Bob fails to publish his hand, then Alice will take her network tokens back.<a href=\"#p_237\" class=\"pid\">237</a>\n</p>\n<p><i id=\"p_238\" class=\"pid\"></i>We will add a similar timeout handler to Alice's second message.<a href=\"#p_238\" class=\"pid\">238</a></p>\n<pre class=\"snippet numbered\"><div class=\"codeHeader\"><a href=\"https://github.com/reach-sh/reach-lang/tree/master/examples/rps-6-timeouts/index.rsh\">/examples/rps-6-timeouts/index.rsh</a><a class=\"far fa-copy copyBtn\" data-clipboard-text=\"  Alice.publish(saltAlice, handAlice)\n    .timeout(relativeTime(deadline), () => closeTo(Bob, informTimeout));\" href=\"#\"></a></div><ol class=\"snippet\"><li value=\"70\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">  </span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-constant)\">Alice</span><a href=\"/rsh/step/#rsh_publish\" title=\"rsh: publish\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-function)\">.publish</span></a><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">(saltAlice</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-punctuation)\">,</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\"> handAlice)</span></li><li value=\"71\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">    </span><a href=\"/rsh/step/#rsh_timeout\" title=\"rsh: timeout\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-function)\">.timeout</span></a><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">(</span><a href=\"/rsh/compute/#rsh_relativeTime\" title=\"rsh: relativeTime\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-function)\">relativeTime</span></a><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">(deadline)</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-punctuation)\">,</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\"> () </span><a href=\"/rsh/compute/#rsh_=%3E\" title=\"rsh: =>\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-keyword)\">=&gt;</span></a><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\"> </span><a href=\"/rsh/step/#rsh_closeTo\" title=\"rsh: closeTo\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-function)\">closeTo</span></a><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">(Bob</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-punctuation)\">,</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\"> informTimeout));</span></li></ol></pre>\n<p>\n  <i id=\"p_239\" class=\"pid\"></i>But in this case, Bob will be able to claim all of the funds if Alice doesn't participate.\n  You might think that it would be \"fair\" for Alice's funds to be returned to Alice and Bob's to Bob.\n  However, if we implemented it that way,\n  then Alice would be wise to always timeout if she were going to lose,\n  which she knows will happen, because she knows her hand and Bob's hand.<a href=\"#p_239\" class=\"pid\">239</a>\n</p>\n<p><i id=\"p_240\" class=\"pid\"></i>These are the only changes we need to make to the Reach program to make it robust against non-participation: eleven lines!<a href=\"#p_240\" class=\"pid\">240</a></p>\n<hr>\n<p><i id=\"p_241\" class=\"pid\"></i>Let's modify the JavaScript frontend to deliberately cause a timeout sometimes when Bob is supposed to accept the wager.<a href=\"#p_241\" class=\"pid\">241</a></p>\n<pre class=\"snippet numbered\"><div class=\"codeHeader\"><a href=\"https://github.com/reach-sh/reach-lang/tree/master/examples/rps-6-timeouts/index.mjs\">/examples/rps-6-timeouts/index.mjs</a><a class=\"far fa-copy copyBtn\" data-clipboard-text=\"await // <-- async now\n      if ( Math.random() <= 0.5 ) {\n        for ( let i = 0; i < 10; i++ ) {\n          console.log(`  Bob takes his sweet time...`);\n          await stdlib.wait(1);\n        }\n style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">deadline</span></span> of ten blocks.<a href=\"#p_242\" class=\"pid\">242</a></li>\n  <li>\n    <i id=\"p_243\" class=\"pid\"></i>Lines 42 through 51 redefine Bob's <span class=\"snip\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">acceptWager</span></span> method as an asynchronous function,\n    where half of the time it will take at least ten blocks on the Ethereum network by waiting for ten units of time to pass.\n    We know that ten is the value of <span class=\"snip\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">deadline</span></span>, so this will cause a timeout.<a href=\"#p_243\" class=\"pid\">243</a>\n  </li>\n</ul>\n<hr>\n<p><i id=\"p_244\" class=\"pid\"></i>Let's run the program and see what happens:<a href=\"#p_244\" var(--shiki-token-constant)\">timeout</span></li><li value=\"42\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">Alice observed a </span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-constant)\">timeout</span></li><li value=\"43\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">Alice went from </span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-constant)\">10</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\"> </span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-keyword)\">to</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\"> </span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-constant)\">9.9999</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">.</span></li><li value=\"44\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">Bob went from </span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-constant)\">10</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\"> </span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-keyword)\">to</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\"> </span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-constant)\">9.9999</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">.</span></li></ol></pre>\n<p><i id=\"p_245\" class=\"pid\"></i>Of course, when you run, you may not get two of the three times ending in a timeout.<a href=\"#p_245\" class=\"pid\">245</a></p>\n<div class=\"note\">\n  <p><i id=\"p_246\" class=\"pid\"></i>If your version isn't working, look at the complete versions of <a href=\"https://github.com/reach-sh/reach-lang/tree/master/examples/rps-6-timeouts/index.rsh\"><code>rps-6-timeouts/index.rsh</code></a> and <a href=\"https://github.com/reach-sh/reach-lang/tree/master/examples/rps-6-timeouts/index.mjs\"><code>rps-6-timeouts/index.mjs</code></a> to make sure you copied everything down correctly!<a href=\"#p_246\" class=\"pid\">246</a></p>\n</div>\n<p>\n  <i id=\"p_247\" class=\"pid\"></i>Now our implementation of <em>Rock, Paper, Scissors!</em> is robust against either participant dropping from the game.\n  In <a href=\"/tut/rps/#tut-7\">the next step</a>, we'll extend the application to disallow draws and have Alice and Bob play again until there is a winner.<a href=\"#p_247\" class=\"pid\">247</a>\n</p>\n<div class=\"q-and-a\" data-bs-toggle=\"collapse\" aria-expanded=\"false\" href=\"#q8\">\n  <p><i id=\"p_248\" class=\"pid\"></i>What happens in a decentralized application when one participant refuses to take the next step of the program? For example, if Alice refuses to share her hand with Bob in a game of Rock, Paper, Scissors.<a href=\"#p_248\" class=\"pid\">248</a></p>\n  <ol>\n    <li><i id=\"p_249\" class=\"pid\"></i>This is not possible, because the blockchain guarantees that each party performs a particular set of actions;<a href=\"#p_249\" class=\"pid\">249</a></li>\n    <li><i id=\"p_250\" class=\"pid\"></i>The program hangs forever waiting for Alice to provide the value;<a href=\"#p_250\" class=\"pid\">250</a></li>\n    <li><i id=\"p_251\" class=\"pid\"></i>Alice is punished and the program proceeds as-if Bob were the winner;<a href=\"#p_251\" class=\"pid\">251</a></li>\n    <li><i id=\"p_252\" class=\"pid\"></i>It depends on how the program was written; if the developer used Reach, the default is (2), but the developer could include a <span class=\"snip\"><a href=\"/rsh/step/#rsh_timeout\" title=\"rsh: timeout\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">timeout</span></a></span> block to implement the (3) behavior.<a href=\"#p_252\" class=\"pid\">252</a></li>\n  </ol>\n  <div class=\"collapse\" id=\"q8\">\n    <p><i id=\"p_253\" class=\"pid\"></i>4; Reach empowers programmers to design the application with the business logic they want.<a href=\"#p_253\" class=\"pid\">253</a></p>\n  </div>\n</div>\n<h2 id=\"tut-7\" class=\"refHeader\">Play and Play Again<a aria-hidden=\"true\" tabindex=\"-1\" href=\"#tut-7\"><span class=\"icon icon-link\"></span></a></h2>\n<p><i id=\"p_254\" class=\"pid\"></i>In this section, we extend our application so that Alice and Bob will continue to play against each other until there is a clear winner, so if it is a draw they will continue playing.<a href=\"#p_254\" class=\"pid\">254</a></p>\n<p>\n  <i id=\"p_255\" class=\"pid\"></i>This will only require a change to the Reach program, not the JavaScript frontend, but we will take the opportunity to modify the frontend so that timeouts can happen to both parties when they are asked to submit their hands.\n  Let's do that to get it out of the way and not distract from the main task of removing draws.<a href=\"#p_255\" class=\"pid\">255</a>\n</p>\n<p><i id=\"p_256\" class=\"pid\"></i>We'll modify the <span class=\"snip\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">Player</span></span> interact object so that it will have a different <span class=\"snip\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">getHand</span></span> method.<a href=\"#p_256\" class=\"pid\">256</a></p>\n<pre class=\"snippet numbered\"><div class=\"codeHeader\"><a 50 have the simpler <span class=\"snip\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">acceptWager</span></span> method for Bob.<a href=\"#p_259\" class=\"pid\">259</a></li>\n</ul>\n<hr>\n<p>\n  <i id=\"p_260\" class=\"pid\"></i>Now, let's look at the Reach application.\n  All of the details about the playing of the game and the interface to the players will remain the same.\n  The only thing that's going to be different is the order the actions take place.<a href=\"#p_260\" class=\"pid\">260</a>\n</p>\n<p><i id=\"p_261\" class=\"pid\"></i>It used to be that the steps were:<a href=\"#p_261\" class=\"pid\">261</a></p>\n<ol>\n  <li><i id=\"p_262\" class=\"pid\"></i>Alice sends her wager and commitment.<a href=\"#p_262\" class=\"pid\">262</a></li>\n  <li><i id=\"p_263\" class=\"pid\"></i>Bob accepts the wager and sends his hand.<a href=\"#p_263\" class=\"pid\">263</a></li>\n  <li><i id=\"p_264\" class=\"pid\"></i>Alice reveals her hand.<a href=\"#p_264\" class=\"pid\">264</a></li>\n  <li><i id=\"p_265\" class=\"pid\"></i>The game ends.<a href=\"#p_265\" class=\"pid\">265</a></li>\n</ol>\n<p><i id=\"p_266\" class=\"pid\"></i>But, now because the players may submit many hands, but should only have a single wager, we'll break these steps up differently, as follows:<a href=\"#p_266\" class=\"pid\">266</a></p>\n<ol>\n  <li><i id=\"p_267\" class=\"pid\"></i>Alice sends her wager.<a href=\"#p_267\" class=\"pid\">267</a></li>\n  <li><i id=\"p_268\" class=\"pid\"></i>Bob accepts the wager.<a href=\"#p_268\" class=\"pid\">268</a></li>\n  <li><i id=\"p_269\" class=\"pid\"></i>Alice sends her commitment.<a href=\"#p_269\" class=\"pid\">269</a></li>\n  <li><i id=\"p_270\" class=\"pid\"></i>Bob sends his hand.<a href=\"#p_270\" class=\"pid\">270</a></li>\n  <li><i id=\"p_271\" class=\"pid\"></i>Alice reveals her hand.<a href=\"#p_271\" class=\"pid\">271</a></li>\n  <li><i id=\"p_272\" class=\"pid\"></i>If it's draw, return to step 3; otherwise, the game ends.<a href=\"#p_272\" class=\"pid\">272</a></li>\n</ol>\n<p><i id=\"p_273\" class=\"pid\"></i>Let's make these changes now.<a href=\"#p_273\" class=\"pid\">273</a></p>\n<pre class=\"snippet numbered\"><div class=\"codeHeader\"><a wager and deadline.<a href=\"#p_274\" class=\"pid\">274</a></li>\n  <li><i id=\"p_275\" class=\"pid\"></i>Line 50 has Alice pay the wager.<a href=\"#p_275\" class=\"pid\">275</a></li>\n</ul>\n<pre class=\"snippet numbered\"><div class=\"codeHeader\"><a href=\"https://github.com/reach-sh/reach-lang/tree/master/examples/rps-7-loops/index.rsh\">/examples/rps-7-loops/index.rsh</a><a class=\"far fa-copy copyBtn\" data-clipboard-text=\"  Bob.only(() => {\n    interact.acceptWager(wager);\n  });\n  Bob.pay(wager)\n    .timeout(relativeTime(deadline), () => closeTo(Alice, informTimeout));\" href=\"#\"></a></div><ol class=\"snippet\"><li value=\"53\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">  </span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-constant)\">Bob</span><a class=\"pid\"></i>Line 56 has Bob pay the wager.<a href=\"#p_276\" class=\"pid\">276</a></li>\n  <li><i id=\"p_277\" class=\"pid\"></i>Line 58 does <strong>not</strong> have this consensus step commit.<a href=\"#p_277\" class=\"pid\">277</a></li>\n</ul>\n<hr>\n<p>\n  <i id=\"p_278\" class=\"pid\"></i>It's now time to begin the repeatable section of the application, where each party will repeatedly submit hands until the the outcome is not a draw.\n  In normal programming languages, such a circumstance would be implemented with a <span class=\"snip\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-keyword)\">while</span></span> loop, which is exactly what we'll do in Reach.\n  However, <span class=\"snip\"><a href=\"/rsh/consensus/#rsh_while\" title=\"rsh: while\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-keyword)\">while</span></a></span> loops in Reach require extra care, as discussed in <a href=\"/guide/loop-invs/#guide-loop-invs\">the guide on loops in Reach</a>, so we'll take it slow.<a href=\"#p_278\" class=\"pid\">278</a>\n</p>\n<p>\n  <i id=\"p_279\" class=\"pid\"></i>In the rest of a Reach program, all identifier bindings are static and unchangeable, but if this were the case throughout all of Reach, then <span class=\"snip\"><a href=\"/rsh/consensus/#rsh_while\" title=\"rsh: while\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-keyword)\">while</span></a></span> loops would either never start or never terminate, because the loop condition would never change.\n  So, a <span class=\"snip\"><a href=\"/rsh/consensus/#rsh_while\" title=\"rsh: while\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-keyword)\">while</span></a></span> loop in Reach can introduce a variable binding.<a href=\"#p_279\" class=\"pid\">279</a>\n</p>\n<p><i id=\"p_280\" class=\"pid\"></i>Next, because of Reach's <a href=\"/guide/assert/#guide-assert\">automatic verification</a> engine, we must be able to make a statement about what properties of the program are invariant before and after a <span class=\"snip\"><a href=\"/rsh/consensus/#rsh_while\" title=\"rsh: while\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-keyword)\">while</span></a></span> loop body's execution, a so-called <a href=\"/guide/loop-invs/#guide-loop-invs\">\"loop invariant\"</a>.<a href=\"#p_280\" class=\"pid\">280</a></p>\n<p>\n  <i id=\"p_281\" class=\"pid\"></i>Finally, such loops <em>may only occur</em> inside of consensus steps.\n  That's why Bob's transaction was not committed, because we need to remain inside of the consensus to start the <span class=\"snip\"><a href=\"/rsh/consensus/#rsh_while\" title=\"rsh: while\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-keyword)\">while</span></a></span> loop.\n  This is because all of the participants must agree on the direction of control flow in the application.<a href=\"#p_281\" class=\"pid\">281</a>\n</p>\n<p><i id=\"p_282\" class=\"pid\"></i>Here's what the structure looks like:<a href=\"#p_282\" class=\"pid\">282</a></p>\n<pre class=\"snippet numbered\"><div title=\"rsh: continue\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-keyword)\">continue</span></a></span> be explicitly written in the loop body.<a href=\"#p_293\" class=\"pid\">293</a>\n  </li>\n</ul>\n<p><i id=\"p_294\" class=\"pid\"></i>The rest of the program could be exactly the same as it was before, except now it occurs outside of the loop, but we will simplify it, because we know that the outcome can never be a draw.<a href=\"#p_294\" class=\"pid\">294</a></p>\n<pre class=\"snippet numbered\"><div class=\"codeHeader\"><a class=\"pid\"></i>As usual, your results may differ, but you should be able to see single round victories like this, as well as multi-round fights and timeouts from either party.<a href=\"#p_298\" class=\"pid\">298</a></p>\n<div class=\"note\">\n  <p><i id=\"p_299\" class=\"pid\"></i>If your version isn't working, look at the complete versions of <a href=\"https://github.com/reach-sh/reach-lang/tree/master/examples/rps-7-loops/index.rsh\"><code>rps-7-loops/index.rsh</code></a> and <a href=\"https://github.com/reach-sh/reach-lang/tree/master/examples/rps-7-loops/index.mjs\"><code>rps-7-loops/index.mjs</code></a> to make sure you copied everything down correctly!<a href=\"#p_299\" class=\"pid\">299</a></p>\n</div>\n<p>\n  <i id=\"p_300\" class=\"pid\"></i>Now our implementation of <em>Rock, Paper, Scissors!</em> will always result in a pay-out, which is much more fun for everyone.\n  In <a href=\"/tut/rps/#tut-8\">the next step</a>, we'll show how to exit \"testing\" mode with Reach and turn our JavaScript into an interactive <em>Rock, Paper, Scissors!</em> game with real users.<a href=\"#p_300\" class=\"pid\">300</a>\n</p>\n<div class=\"q-and-a\" data-bs-toggle=\"collapse\" aria-expanded=\"false\" href=\"#q9\">\n  <p><i id=\"p_301\" class=\"pid\"></i>How do you write an application in Reach that runs arbitrarily long, like a game of Rock, Paper, Scissors that is guaranteed to not end in a draw?<a href=\"#p_301\" class=\"pid\">301</a></p>\n  <ol>\n    <li><i id=\"p_302\" class=\"pid\"></i>This is not possible, because all Reach programs are finitely long;<a href=\"#p_302\" class=\"pid\">302</a></li>\n    <li><i id=\"p_303\" class=\"pid\"></i>You can use a <span class=\"snip\"><a href=\"/rsh/consensus/#rsh_while\" title=\"rsh: while\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-keyword)\">while</span></a></span> loop that runs until the outcome of the game is decided.<a href=\"#p_303\" class=\"pid\">303</a></li>\n  </ol>\n  <div class=\"collapse\" id=\"q9\">\n    <p><i id=\"p_304\" class=\"pid\"></i>2; Reach supports <span class=\"snip\"><a href=\"/rsh/consensus/#rsh_while\" title=\"rsh: while\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-keyword)\">while</span></a></span> loops.<a href=\"#p_304\" class=\"pid\">304</a></p>\n  </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"q-and-a\" data-bs-toggle=\"collapse\" aria-expanded=\"false\" href=\"#q10\">\n  <p><i id=\"p_305\" class=\"pid\"></i>When you check if a program with a <span class=\"snip\"><a href=\"/rsh/consensus/#rsh_while\" title=\"rsh: while\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-keyword)\">while</span></a></span> loop is correct, you need to have a property called a loop invariant. Which of the following statements have to be true about the loop invariant?<a href=\"#p_305\" class=\"pid\">305</a></p>\n  <ol>\n    <li>\n      <p><i id=\"p_306\" class=\"pid\"></i>The part of the program before the <span class=\"snip\"><a href=\"/rsh/consensus/#rsh_while\" title=\"rsh: while\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-keyword)\">while</span></a></span> loop must establish the invariant.<a href=\"#p_306\" class=\"pid\">306</a></p>\n    </li>\n    <li>\n      <p><i id=\"p_307\" class=\"pid\"></i>The condition and the body of the loop must establish the invariant.<a href=\"#p_307\" class=\"pid\">307</a></p>\n    </li>\n    <li>\n      <p><i id=\"p_308\" class=\"pid\"></i>The negation of the condition and the invariant must establish any properties of the rest of the program.<a href=\"#p_308\" class=\"pid\">308</a></p>\n    </li>\n  </ol>\n  <div class=\"collapse\" id=\"q10\">\n    <p><i id=\"p_309\" class=\"pid\"></i>All of the above.<a href=\"#p_309\" class=\"pid\">309</a></p>\n  </div>\n</div>\n<h2 id=\"tut-8\" class=\"refHeader\">Interaction and Independence<a aria-hidden=\"true\" tabindex=\"-1\" href=\"#tut-8\"><span class=\"icon icon-link\"></span></a></h2>\n<p>\n  <i id=\"p_310\" class=\"pid\"></i>In the last section, we made our <em>Rock, Paper, Scissors!</em> run until there was a definitive winner.\n  In this section, we won't be making any changes to the Reach program itself.\n  Instead, we'll introduce customizations to the JavaScript frontend which facilitate interactivity and provide the option to connect to a real consensus network.<a href=\"#p_310\" class=\"pid\">310</a>\n</p>\n<hr>\n<p>\n  <i id=\"p_311\" class=\"pid\"></i>We'll start from scratch and show every line of the program again.\n  You'll see a lot of similarity between this and the last version, but for completeness, we'll show every line.<a href=\"#p_311\" class=\"pid\">311</a>\n</p>\n<pre class=\"snippet numbered\"><div class=\"pid\">335</a></p>\n<p><i id=\"p_336\" class=\"pid\"></i>Connecting to live consensus networks is similarly easy:<a href=\"#p_336\" class=\"pid\">336</a></p>\n<pre class=\"snippet href=\"#\"></a></div><ol class=\"snippet\"><li value=\"1\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-keyword)\">$</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\"> REACH_CONNECTOR_MODE</span><span var(--shiki-token-string-expression)\">\"http://some.node.fqdn:8545\"</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\"> ./reach run</span></li></ol></pre>\n<hr>\n<p>\n  <i id=\"p_337\" class=\"pid\"></i>Now our implementation of <em>Rock, Paper, Scissors!</em> is finished!\n  We are protected against attacks, timeouts, and draws, and we can run interactively on non-test networks.<a href=\"#p_337\" class=\"pid\">337</a>\n</p>\n<p>\n  <i id=\"p_338\" class=\"pid\"></i>In this step, we made a command-line interface for our Reach program.\n  In <a href=\"/tut/rps/#tut-9\">the next step</a>, we'll replace this with a Web interface for the same Reach program.<a href=\"#p_338\" class=\"pid\">338</a>\n</p>\n<div class=\"q-and-a\" data-bs-toggle=\"collapse\" aria-expanded=\"false\" href=\"#q11\">\n  <p><i id=\"p_339\" class=\"pid\"></i>Reach helps you build automated tests for your decentralized application, but it doesnt support building interactive user-interfaces.<a href=\"#p_339\" class=\"pid\">339</a></p>\n  <div class=\"collapse\" id=\"q11\">\n    <p><i id=\"p_340\" class=\"pid\"></i>False; Reach does not impose any constraints on what kind of frontend is attached to your Reach application.<a href=\"#p_340\" class=\"pid\">340</a></p>\n  </div>\n</div>\n<h2 id=\"tut-9\" class=\"refHeader\">Web Interaction<a aria-hidden=\"true\" tabindex=\"-1\" href=\"#tut-9\"><span class=\"icon icon-link\"></span></a></h2>\n<p>\n  <i id=\"p_341\" class=\"pid\"></i>In the last section, we made <em>Rock, Paper, Scissors!</em> run as a command-line application, without any changes to the Reach program.\n  In this section, we again won't be making any changes to the Reach program.\n  Instead, we'll replace the command-line interface with a Web interface.<a href=\"#p_341\" class=\"pid\">341</a>\n</p>\n<p><i id=\"p_342\" class=\"pid\"></i>We will use <a href=\"https://reactjs.org/\">React.js</a> for this tutorial, but the same principles apply to any Web framework.<a href=\"#p_342\" class=\"pid\">342</a></p>\n<div class=\"note\">\n  <p><i id=\"p_343\" class=\"pid\"></i>If you've never used React before, here are some basics about how it works:<a href=\"#p_343\" class=\"pid\">343</a></p>\n  <ul>\n    <li><i id=\"p_344\" class=\"pid\"></i>React programs are JavaScript programs that use a special library that allows you to mix HTML inside of the body of your JavaScript.<a href=\"#p_344\" class=\"pid\">344</a></li>\n    <li>\n      <i id=\"p_345\" class=\"pid\"></i>React has a special compiler that combines a bundle of JavaScript programs, and all their dependencies, into one large file that can be deployed on a static Web server.\n      This is called \"packing\".<a href=\"#p_345\" class=\"pid\">345</a>\n    </li>\n    <li><i id=\"p_346\" class=\"pid\"></i>When you're developing and testing with React, you run a special development Web server that watches and updates this packed file every time you modify a source file, so you don't have to constantly run the compiler.<a href=\"#p_346\" class=\"pid\">346</a></li>\n    <li><i id=\"p_347\" class=\"pid\"></i>Reach automates the process of starting this development server for you when you run <code>./reach react</code> and gives you access to it at <code>http://localhost:3000/</code>.<a href=\"#p_347\" class=\"pid\">347</a></li>\n  </ul>\n</div>\n<p>\n  <i id=\"p_348\" class=\"pid\"></i>Similarly, in this tutorial, we assume that we will be deploying (and testing) with Ethereum.\n  Reach Web applications rely on the Web browser to provide access to a consensus network account and its associated wallet.\n  On Ethereum, the standard wallet is <a href=\"https://metamask.io\">MetaMask</a>.\n  If you want to test this code, you'll need to install it and set it up.\n  Furthermore, MetaMask does not support multiple active accounts, so if you want to test <em>Rock, Paper, Scissors!</em> locally, you'll need to have two separate browser instances: one to act as Alice and another to act as Bob.<a href=\"#p_348\" class=\"pid\">348</a>\n</p>\n<p><i id=\"p_349\" class=\"pid\"></i>To complete this section we'll use the <code>index.rsh</code> you've already written and create an <code>index.js</code> file from scratch which replaces <code>index.mjs</code>.<a href=\"#p_349\" class=\"pid\">349</a></p>\n<div class=\"note\">\n  <p>\n    <i id=\"p_350\" class=\"pid\"></i>If you do not replace <code>index.mjs</code>, then you will get an error when you run <code>reach react</code>.\n    You can avoid this error by renaming the file to <code>index.mjs.bak</code>, or by creating a totally new directory with a copy of the old <code>index.rsh.</code>\n    We do the second option.<a href=\"#p_350\" class=\"pid\">350</a>\n  </p>\n</div>\n<p>\n  <i id=\"p_351\" class=\"pid\"></i>This code is also supplemented with <a href=\"https://github.com/reach-sh/reach-lang/tree/master/examples/rps-9-web/index.css\">index.css</a>\n  and some <a href=\"https://github.com/reach-sh/reach-lang/tree/master/examples/rps-9-web/views\">views</a>.\n  These details are not specific to Reach, and are fairly trivial,\n  so we will not explain the specifics of those files.\n  If you run this locally, you'll want to download those files.\n  Your directory should look like:<a href=\"#p_351\" class=\"pid\">351</a>\n</p>\n<pre class=\"snippet numbered\"><div class=\"codeHeader\">&nbsp;<a class=\"far fa-copy copyBtn\" data-clipboard-text=\".\n index.css\n index.js\n index.rsh\n views\n     AppViews.js\n id=\"p_354\" class=\"pid\"></i>React compiles the Reach standard library in such a way that\n  it does not have direct access to the environment variables\n  which are used to select the desired standard library.\n  This is why you need to pass <span class=\"snip\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-constant)\">process</span><span style=\"color: Terms and Pay Wager</code> button:\n    the <span class=\"snip\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-constant)\">Promise</span></span> from line 90 is resolved, and we set the component state to display <a href=\"/tut/rps/#tut-9-WaitingForTurn\">Waiting for Turn display</a>.<a href=\"#p_412\" class=\"pid\">412</a>\n  </li>\n  <li><i id=\"p_413\" class=\"pid\"></i>On line 93, we render the appropriate view from <a href=\"https://github.com/reach-sh/reach-lang/tree/master/examples/rps-9-web/views/AttacherViews.js\">rps-9-web/views/AttacherViews.js</a><a href=\"#p_413\" class=\"pid\">413</a></li>\n</ul>\n<h3 id=\"tut-9-Attach\" class=\"refHeader\">Attach dialog<a aria-hidden=\"true\" tabindex=\"-1\" href=\"#tut-9-Attach\"><span class=\"icon href=\"https://github.com/reach-sh/reach-lang/tree/master/examples/rps-9-web/views/AttacherViews.js#L18-L39\">rps-9-web/views/AttacherViews.js</a>) looks like:\n  \n  <img src=\"/tut/rps/./rps-9-web/Attach.png\" alt=\"\"><a href=\"#p_414\" class=\"pid\">414</a>\n</p>\n<h3 id=\"tut-9-Attaching\" class=\"refHeader\">Attaching display<a aria-hidden=\"true\" tabindex=\"-1\" href=\"https://github.com/reach-sh/reach-lang/tree/master/examples/rps-9-web/index.js\">/examples/rps-9-web/index.js</a><a class=\"far fa-copy copyBtn\" data-clipboard-text=\"renderDOM(<App />);\" href=\"#\"></a></div><ol class=\"snippet\"><li value=\"96\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-function)\">renderDOM</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">(&lt;</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-constant)\">App</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\"> /&gt;);</span></li></ol></pre>\n<p>\n  <i id=\"p_418\" class=\"pid\"></i>Finally, we call a small helper function from <a href=\"https://github.com/reach-sh/reach-lang/tree/master/examples/rps-9-web/views/render.js\">rps-9-web/views/render.js</a>\n  to render our App component.<a href=\"#p_418\" class=\"pid\">418</a>\n</p>\n<hr>\n<p>\n  <i id=\"p_419\" class=\"pid\"></i>As a convenience for running the React development server,\n  you can call:<a href=\"#p_419\" class=\"pid\">419</a>\n</p>\n<pre class=\"snippet unnumbered\"><div class=\"codeHeader\">&nbsp;<a class=\"far fa-copy copyBtn\" data-clipboard-text=\"./reach react\" href=\"#\"></a></div><ol class=\"snippet\"><li value=\"1\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-keyword)\">$</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\"> ./reach react</span></li></ol></pre>\n<div class=\"note\">\n  <p>\n    <i id=\"p_420\" class=\"pid\"></i>If you get an error or it does not seem to be working correctly, make sure that the folder does not have an <code>index.mjs</code> file.\n    If you do, you can rename it to <code>index.mjs.bak</code> or move it to a new directory with a copy of the old <code>index.rsh</code>.<a href=\"#p_420\" class=\"pid\">420</a>\n  </p>\n</div>\n<hr>\n<p>\n  <i id=\"p_421\" class=\"pid\"></i>To run the React development server with Algorand,\n  you can call:<a href=\"#p_421\" class=\"pid\">421</a>\n</p>\n<pre class=\"snippet unnumbered\"><div class=\"codeHeader\">&nbsp;<a class=\"far fa-copy copyBtn\" data-clipboard-text=\"REACH_CONNECTOR_MODE=ALGO ./reach react\" href=\"#\"></a></div><ol class=\"snippet\"><li value=\"1\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-keyword)\">$</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\"> REACH_CONNECTOR_MODE</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-keyword)\">=</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">ALGO ./reach react</span></li></ol></pre>\n<div class=\"note\">\n  <p><i id=\"p_422\" class=\"pid\"></i>If you expect that your Algorand users do not have access to an <a href=\"https://github.com/algorandfoundation/ARCs/blob/main/ARCs/arc-0011.md\">ARC-0011</a> browser wallet, you want to provide a fallback.<a href=\"#p_422\" class=\"pid\">422</a></p>\n  <p><i id=\"p_423\" class=\"pid\"></i>If you add the following to your program, then you can provide a simple wallet where the user copies and pastes their mnemonic for each interaction.<a href=\"#p_423\" class=\"pid\">423</a></p>\n  <pre class=\"snippet unnumbered\"><div class=\"codeHeader\">&nbsp;<a class=\"far fa-copy copyBtn\" data-clipboard-text=\"reach.setWalletFallback(reach.walletFallback({}));\" href=\"#\"></a></div><ol class=\"snippet\"><li value=\"1\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-constant)\">reach</span><a href=\"/frontend/#js_setWalletFallback\" title=\"js: setWalletFallback\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-function)\">.setWalletFallback</span></a><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">(</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-constant)\">reach</span><a href=\"/frontend/#js_walletFallback\" title=\"js: walletFallback\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-function)\">.walletFallback</span></a><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">({}));</span></li></ol></pre>\n  <p><i id=\"p_424\" class=\"pid\"></i>Instead, if you would like to allow your users to use <a href=\"https://wallet.myalgo.com/home\">MyAlgo</a>, then you can add the following:<a href=\"#p_424\" class=\"pid\">424</a></p>\n  <pre class=\"snippet numbered\"><div class=\"codeHeader\">&nbsp;<a class=\"far fa-copy copyBtn\" data-clipboard-text=\"import { ALGO_MyAlgoConnect as MyAlgoConnect } from '@reach-sh/stdlib';\nreach.setWalletFallback(reach.walletFallback({\n  providerEnv: 'TestNet', MyAlgoConnect }));\" href=\"#\"></a></div><ol class=\"snippet\"><li value=\"1\"><a href=\"https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Statements/import\" title=\"js: import\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-keyword)\">import</span></a><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\"> { ALGO_MyAlgoConnect </span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-keyword)\">as</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\"> MyAlgoConnect } </span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-keyword)\">from</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\"> </span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-string-expression)\">'@reach-sh/stdlib'</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">;</span></li><li value=\"2\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-constant)\">reach</span><a href=\"/frontend/#js_setWalletFallback\" title=\"js: setWalletFallback\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-function)\">.setWalletFallback</span></a><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">(</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-constant)\">reach</span><a href=\"/frontend/#js_walletFallback\" title=\"js: walletFallback\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-function)\">.walletFallback</span></a><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">({</span></li><li value=\"3\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">  providerEnv</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-keyword)\">:</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\"> </span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-string-expression)\">'TestNet'</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-punctuation)\">,</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\"> MyAlgoConnect }));</span></li></ol></pre>\n  <p><i id=\"p_425\" class=\"pid\"></i>Or, you could have your users use <a href=\"https://walletconnect.com/\">WalletConnect</a> to connect to the <a href=\"https://algorandwallet.com/\">Algorand Wallet</a>, by adding the following:<a href=\"#p_425\" class=\"pid\">425</a></p>\n  <pre class=\"snippet numbered\"><div class=\"codeHeader\">&nbsp;<a class=\"far fa-copy copyBtn\" data-clipboard-text=\"import { ALGO_WalletConnect as WalletConnect } from '@reach-sh/stdlib';\nreach.setWalletFallback(reach.walletFallback({\n  providerEnv: 'TestNet', WalletConnect }));\" href=\"#\"></a></div><ol class=\"snippet\"><li value=\"1\"><a href=\"https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Statements/import\" title=\"js: import\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-keyword)\">import</span></a><span these samples with a different network name, like <code>'MainNet'</code>.)<a href=\"#p_426\" class=\"pid\">426</a></p>\n  <p><i id=\"p_427\" class=\"pid\"></i>Because these are fallbacks, you need to decide for your users which wallet they'll use, or make a user interface element to let them select which wallet fallback to use.<a href=\"#p_427\" class=\"pid\">427</a></p>\n</div>\n<p><i id=\"p_428\" class=\"pid\"></i>Similarly, to run with Conflux:<a href=\"#p_428\" class=\"pid\">428</a></p>\n<pre class=\"snippet unnumbered\"><div class=\"codeHeader\">&nbsp;<a class=\"far fa-copy react</span></li></ol></pre>\n<div class=\"note\">\n  <p>\n    <i id=\"p_429\" class=\"pid\"></i>To adapt this example for Conflux TestNet or MainNet,\n    you can add this after the imports:<a href=\"#p_430\" class=\"pid\">430</a></p>\n</div>\n<hr>\n<p>\n  <i id=\"p_431\" class=\"pid\"></i>If you'd like to instead use Reach in your own JavaScript project,\n  you can call:<a href=\"#p_431\" class=\"pid\">431</a>\n</p>\n<pre class=\"snippet unnumbered\"><div class=\"codeHeader\">&nbsp;<a class=\"far fa-copy copyBtn\" data-clipboard-text=\"npm install @reach-sh/stdlib\" href=\"#\"></a></div><ol class=\"snippet\"><li value=\"1\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-keyword)\">$</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\"> npm install @reach</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-keyword)\">-</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">sh/stdlib</span></li></ol></pre>\n<div class=\"note\">\n  <p>\n    <i id=\"p_432\" class=\"pid\"></i>The Reach standard library is undergoing continual improvement and is updated often.\n    If you are experiencing issues with the Node.js package, try updating!<a href=\"#p_432\" class=\"pid\">432</a>\n  </p>\n</div>\n<p><i id=\"p_433\" class=\"pid\"></i>As usual, you can compile your Reach program <code>index.rsh</code> to the <span class=\"snip\"><a href=\"/cout/#js_backend\" title=\"js: backend\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\">backend</span></a></span> build artifact <code>build/index.main.mjs</code> with:<a href=\"#p_433\" class=\"pid\">433</a></p>\n<pre class=\"snippet unnumbered\"><div class=\"codeHeader\">&nbsp;<a class=\"far fa-copy copyBtn\" data-clipboard-text=\"./reach compile\" href=\"#\"></a></div><ol class=\"snippet\"><li value=\"1\"><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-token-keyword)\">$</span><span style=\"color: var(--shiki-color-text)\"> ./reach compile</span></li></ol></pre>\n<hr>\n<p>\n  <i id=\"p_434\" class=\"pid\"></i>Now our implementation of <em>Rock, Paper, Scissors!</em> is live in the browser!\n  We can leverage callbacks in the participant interact interface to display to and gather information from the user,\n  through any Web UI framework of our choice.<a href=\"#p_434\" class=\"pid\">434</a>\n</p>\n<p>\n  <i id=\"p_435\" class=\"pid\"></i>If we wanted to deploy this application to the world, then we would take the static files that React produces and host them on a Web server.\n  These files embed your compiled Reach program, so there's nothing more to do than provide them to the world.<a href=\"#p_435\" class=\"pid\">435</a>\n</p>\n<p><i id=\"p_436\" class=\"pid\"></i>In <a href=\"/tut/rps/#tut-10\">the next section</a>, we'll summarize where we've gone and direct you to the next step of your journey to decentralized application mastery.<a href=\"#p_436\" class=\"pid\">436</a></p>\n<div class=\"q-and-a\" data-bs-toggle=\"collapse\" aria-expanded=\"false\" href=\"#q12\">\n  <p><i id=\"p_437\" class=\"pid\"></i>Reach integrates with all Web interface libraries, like React, Vue, and so on, because Reach frontends are just normal JavaScript programs.<a href=\"#p_437\" class=\"pid\">437</a></p>\n  <div class=\"collapse\" id=\"q12\">\n    <p><i id=\"p_438\" class=\"pid\"></i>True<a href=\"#p_438\" class=\"pid\">438</a></p>\n  </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"q-and-a\" data-bs-toggle=\"collapse\" aria-expanded=\"false\" href=\"#q13\">\n  <p><i id=\"p_439\" class=\"pid\"></i>Reach accelerates your development with React by baking-in a React development server and the deployment process to test React programs locally.<a href=\"#p_439\" class=\"pid\">439</a></p>\n  <div class=\"collapse\" id=\"q13\">\n    <p><i id=\"p_440\" class=\"pid\"></i>True<a href=\"#p_440\" class=\"pid\">440</a></p>\n  </div>\n</div>\n<h2 id=\"tut-10\" class=\"refHeader\">Onward and Further<a aria-hidden=\"true\" tabindex=\"-1\" href=\"#tut-10\"><span class=\"icon icon-link\"></span></a></h2>\n<p><i id=\"p_441\" class=\"pid\"></i>Let's review what we've done through this tutorial:<a href=\"#p_441\" class=\"pid\">441</a></p>\n<ul>\n  <li><i id=\"p_442\" class=\"pid\"></i>In <a href=\"/tut/rps/#tut-1\">part one</a>, we saw how Reach can be installed with one command on almost any system without any dependencies beyond what most developers have anyways.<a href=\"#p_442\" class=\"pid\">442</a></li>\n  <li><i id=\"p_443\" class=\"pid\"></i>In <a href=\"/tut/rps/#tut-2\">part two</a>, we saw how Reach programs have a succinct setup that easily abstracts the details of your chosen consensus network into a couple lines and three key API calls.<a href=\"#p_443\" class=\"pid\">443</a></li>\n  <li><i id=\"p_444\" class=\"pid\"></i>In <a href=\"/tut/rps/#tut-3\">part three</a>, we saw how Reach allows developers to focus on the business logic of their decentralized application and look past the nitty-gritty details of blockchain interaction and protocol design.<a href=\"#p_444\" class=\"pid\">444</a></li>\n  <li><i id=\"p_445\" class=\"pid\"></i>In <a href=\"/tut/rps/#tut-4\">part four</a>, we saw that it is just as easy for Reach to deal with tokens and network transactions as it is to deal with data sharing.<a href=\"#p_445\" class=\"pid\">445</a></li>\n  <li><i id=\"p_446\" class=\"pid\"></i>In <a href=\"/tut/rps/#tut-5\">part five</a>, we introduced you to the Reach <a href=\"/guide/assert/#guide-assert\">automatic formal verification</a> engine and its ability to ensure our program doesn't have entire categories of flaws and security vulnerabilities.<a href=\"#p_446\" class=\"pid\">446</a></li>\n  <li><i id=\"p_447\" class=\"pid\"></i>In <a href=\"/tut/rps/#tut-6\">part six</a>, we saw how Reach allows you to specify how to deal with <a href=\"/guide/timeout/#guide-timeout\">non-participation</a> and protect against funds being locked in contracts.<a href=\"#p_447\" class=\"pid\">447</a></li>\n  <li><i id=\"p_448\" class=\"pid\"></i>In <a href=\"/tut/rps/#tut-7\">part seven</a>, we saw how Reach can express arbitrary length interactions and how flexible the Reach frontends are to variations in the backend.<a href=\"#p_448\" class=\"pid\">448</a></li>\n  <li><i id=\"p_449\" class=\"pid\"></i>In <a href=\"/tut/rps/#tut-8\">part eight</a>, we saw how to decouple your Reach program from the Reach standard testing environment and launch an interactive version on a real network.<a href=\"#p_449\" class=\"pid\">449</a></li>\n  <li><i id=\"p_450\" class=\"pid\"></i>In <a href=\"/tut/rps/#tut-9\">part nine</a>, we saw how to deploy your Reach program as a fully decentralized Web application.<a href=\"#p_450\" class=\"pid\">450</a></li>\n</ul>\n<p><i id=\"p_451\" class=\"pid\"></i>Despite having done so much, this is really just a brief introduction to what is possible with Reach.<a href=\"#p_451\" class=\"pid\">451</a></p>\n<p>\n  <i id=\"p_452\" class=\"pid\"></i>How difficult was all this?\n  Let's look at the final versions of our programs.<a href=\"#p_452\" class=\"pid\">452</a>\n</p>\n<p><i id=\"p_453\" class=\"pid\"></i>First, let's look at the Reach program:<a href=\"#p_453\" class=\"pid\">453</a></p>\n<pre class=\"snippet numbered\"><div class=\"codeHeader\"><a href=\"https://github.com/reach-sh/reach-lang/tree/master/examples/rps-8-interact/index.rsh\">/examples/rps-8-interact/index.rsh</a><a class=\"far fa-copy copyBtn\" data-clipboard-text=\"'reach 0.1';\n\nconst [ isHand, ROCK, PAPER, SCISSORS ] = makeEnum(3);\nconst [ isOutcome, B_WINS, DRAW, A_WINS ] = makeEnum(3);\n\nconst winner = (handAlice, handBob) =>\n  ((handAlice + (4 - handBob)) % 3);\n\nassert(winner(ROCK, PAPER) == B_WINS);\nassert(winner(PAPER, ROCK) == A_WINS);\nassert(winner(ROCK, ROCK) == DRAW);\n\nforall(UInt, handAlice =>\n  forall(UInt, handBob =>\n    assert(isOutcome(winner(handAlice, handBob)))));\n\nforall(UInt, (hand) =>\n  assert(winner(hand, hand) == DRAW));\n\nconst Player = {\n  ...hasRandom,\n  getHand: Fun([], UInt),\n  seeOutcome: Fun([UInt], Null),\n  informTimeout: Fun([], Null),\n};\n\nexport const main = Reach.App(() => {\n  const Alice = Participant('Alice', {\n    ...Player,\n    wager: UInt, // atomic units of currency\n    deadline: UInt, // time delta (blocks/rounds)\n  });\n  const Bob   = Participant('Bob', {\n    ...Player,\n    acceptWager: Fun([UInt], Null),\n  });\n  init();\n\n  const informTimeout = () => {\n    each([Alice, Bob], () => {\n      interact.informTimeout();\n    });\n  };\n\n  Alice.only(() => {\n    const wager = declassify(interact.wager);\n    const deadline = declassify(interact.deadline);\n  });\n  Alice.publish(wager, deadline)\n    .pay(wager);\n  commit();\n\n  Bob.only(() => {\n    interact.acceptWager(wager);\n  });\n  Bob.pay(wager)\n    .timeout(relativeTime(deadline), () => closeTo(Alice, informTimeout));\n\n  var outcome = DRAW;\n  invariant( balance() == 2 * wager &amp;&amp; isOutcome(outcome) );\n  while ( outcome == DRAW ) {\n    commit();\n\n    Alice.only(() => {\n      const _handAlice = interact.getHand();\n      const [_commitAlice, _saltAlice] = makeCommitment(interact, _handAlice);\n      const commitAlice = declassify(_commitAlice);\n    });\n    Alice.publish(commitAlice)\n      .timeout(relativeTime(deadline), () => closeTo(Bob, informTimeout));\n    commit();\n\n    unknowable(Bob, Alice(_handAlice, _saltAlice));\n    Bob.only(() => {\n      const handBob = declassify(interact.getHand());\n    });\n    Bob.publish(handBob)\n      .timeout(relativeTime(deadline), () => closeTo(Alice, informTimeout));\n    commit();\n\n    Alice.only(() => {\n      const saltAlice = declassify(_saltAlice);\n      const handAlice = declassify(_handAlice);\n    });\n    Alice.publish(saltAlice, handAlice)\n      .timeout(relativeTime(deadline), () => closeTo(Bob, informTimeout));\n    checkCommitment(commitAlice, saltAlice, handAlice);\n\n    outcome = winner(handAlice, handBob);\n    continue;\n  }\n\n  assert(outcome == A_WINS || outcome == B_WINS);\n  transfer(2 * wager).to(outcome == A_WINS ? Alice : Bob);\n  commit();\n\n  each([Alice, Bob], () => {\n    interact.seeOutcome(outcome);\n  });\n});\" href=\"#\"></a></div><ol class=\"snippet\"><li value=\"1\"><span style=\"color: loadStdlib, ask } from '@reach-sh/stdlib';\nimport * as backend from './build/index.main.mjs';\nconst stdlib = loadStdlib();\n\nconst isAlice = await ask.ask(\n  `Are you Alice?`,\n  ask.yesno\n);\nconst who = isAlice ? 'Alice' : 'Bob';\n\nconsole.log(`Starting Rock, Paper, Scissors! as ${who}`);\n\nlet acc = null;\nconst createAcc = await ask.ask(\n  `Would you like to create an account? (only possible on devnet)`,\n  ask.yesno\n);\nif (createAcc) {\n  acc = await stdlib.newTestAccount(stdlib.parseCurrency(1000));\n} else {\n  const secret = await ask.ask(\n    `What is your account secret?`,\n    (x => x)\n  );\n  acc = await stdlib.newAccountFromSecret(secret);\n}\n\nlet ctc = null;\nif (isAlice) {\n  ctc = acc.contract(backend);\n  ctc.getInfo().then((info) => {\n    console.log(`The contract is deployed as = ${JSON.stringify(info)}`); });\n} else {\n  const info = await ask.ask(\n    `Please paste the contract information:`,\n    JSON.parse\n  );\n  ctc = acc.contract(backend, info);\n}\n\nconst fmt = (x) => stdlib.formatCurrency(x, 4);\nconst getBalance = async () => fmt(await stdlib.balanceOf(acc));\n\nconst before = await getBalance();\nconsole.log(`Your balance is ${before}`);\n\nconst interact = { ...stdlib.hasRandom };\n\ninteract.informTimeout = () => {\n  console.log(`There was a timeout.`);\n  process.exit(1);\n};\n\nif (isAlice) {\n  const amt = await ask.ask(\n    `How much do you want to wager?`,\n    stdlib.parseCurrency\n  );\n  interact.wager = amt;\n  interact.deadline = { ETH: 100, ALGO: 100, CFX: 1000 }[stdlib.connector];\n} else {\n  interact.acceptWager = async (amt) => {\n    const accepted = await ask.ask(\n      `Do you accept the wager of ${fmt(amt)}?`,\n      ask.yesno\n    );\n    if (!accepted) {\n      process.exit(0);\n    }\n  };\n}\n\nconst HAND = ['Rock', 'Paper', 'Scissors'];\nconst HANDS = {\n  'Rock': 0, 'R': 0, 'r': 0,\n  'Paper': 1, 'P': 1, 'p': 1,\n  'Scissors': 2, 'S': 2, 's': 2,\n};\n\ninteract.getHand = async () => {\n  const hand = await ask.ask(`What hand will you play?`, (x) => {\n    const hand = HANDS[x];\n    if ( hand === undefined ) {\n      throw Error(`Not a valid hand ${hand}`);\n    }\n    return hand;\n  });\n  console.log(`You played ${HAND[hand]}`);\n  return hand;\n};\n\nconst OUTCOME = ['Bob wins', 'Draw', 'Alice wins'];\ninteract.seeOutcome = async (outcome) => {\n  console.log(`The outcome is: ${OUTCOME[outcome]}`);\n};\n\nconst part = isAlice ? ctc.p.Alice : ctc.p.Bob;\nawait part(interact);\n\nconst after = await getBalance();\nconsole.log(`Your balance is now ${after}`);\n\nask.done();\" href=\"#\"></a></div><ol class=\"snippet\"><li value=\"1\"><a class=\"pid\"></i>And finally, the Web frontend:<a href=\"#p_455\" class=\"pid\">455</a></p>\n<pre class=\"snippet numbered\"><div class=\"codeHeader\"><a href=\"https://github.com/reach-sh/reach-lang/tree/master/examples/rps-9-web/index.js\">/examples/rps-9-web/index.js</a><a class=\"far fa-copy copyBtn\" data-clipboard-text=\"import React from 'react';\nimport AppViews from './views/AppViews';\nimport DeployerViews from './views/DeployerViews';\nimport AttacherViews from './views/AttacherViews';\nimport {renderDOM, renderView} from './views/render';\nimport './index.css';\nimport * as backend from './build/index.main.mjs';\nimport { loadStdlib } from '@reach-sh/stdlib';\nconst reach = loadStdlib(process.env);\n\nconst handToInt = {'ROCK': 0, 'PAPER': 1, 'SCISSORS': 2};\nconst intToOutcome = ['Bob wins!', 'Draw!', 'Alice wins!'];\nconst {standardUnit} = reach;\nconst defaults = {defaultFundAmt: '10', defaultWager: '3', standardUnit};\n\nclass App extends React.Component {\n  constructor(props) {\n    super(props);\n    this.state = {view: 'ConnectAccount', ...defaults};\n  }\n  async componentDidMount() {\n    const acc = await reach.getDefaultAccount();\n    const balAtomic = await reach.balanceOf(acc);\n    const bal = reach.formatCurrency(balAtomic, 4);\n    this.setState({acc, bal});\n    if (await reach.canFundFromFaucet()) {\n      this.setState({view: 'FundAccount'});\n    } else {\n      this.setState({view: 'DeployerOrAttacher'});\n    }\n  }\n  async fundAccount(fundAmount) {\n    await reach.fundFromFaucet(this.state.acc, reach.parseCurrency(fundAmount));\n    this.setState({view: 'DeployerOrAttacher'});\n  }\n  async skipFundAccount() { this.setState({view: 'DeployerOrAttacher'}); }\n  selectAttacher() { this.setState({view: 'Wrapper', ContentView: Attacher}); }\n  selectDeployer() { this.setState({view: 'Wrapper', ContentView: Deployer}); }\n  render() { return renderView(this, AppViews); }\n}\n\nclass Player extends React.Component {\n  random() { return reach.hasRandom.random(); }\n  async getHand() { // Fun([], UInt)\n    const hand = await new Promise(resolveHandP => {\n      this.setState({view: 'GetHand', playable: true, resolveHandP});\n    });\n    this.setState({view: 'WaitingForResults', hand});\n    return handToInt[hand];\n  }\n  seeOutcome(i) { this.setState({view: 'Done', outcome: intToOutcome[i]}); }\n  informTimeout() { this.setState({view: 'Timeout'}); }\n  playHand(hand) { this.state.resolveHandP(hand); }\n}\n\nclass Deployer extends Player {\n  constructor(props) {\n    super(props);\n    this.state = {view: 'SetWager'};\n  }\n  setWager(wager) { this.setState({view: 'Deploy', wager}); }\n  async deploy() {\n    const ctc = this.props.acc.contract(backend);\n    this.setState({view: 'Deploying', ctc});\n    this.wager = reach.parseCurrency(this.state.wager); // UInt\n    this.deadline = {ETH: 10, ALGO: 100, CFX: 1000}[reach.connector]; // UInt\n    backend.Alice(ctc, this);\n    const ctcInfoStr = JSON.stringify(await ctc.getInfo(), null, 2);\n    this.setState({view: 'WaitingForAttacher', ctcInfoStr});\n  }\n  render() { return renderView(this, DeployerViews); }\n}\nclass Attacher extends Player {\n  constructor(props) {\n    super(props);\n    this.state = {view: 'Attach'};\n  }\n  attach(ctcInfoStr) {\n    const ctc = this.props.acc.contract(backend, JSON.parse(ctcInfoStr));\n    this.setState({view: 'Attaching'});\n    backend.Bob(ctc, this);\n  }\n  async acceptWager(wagerAtomic) { // Fun([UInt], Null)\n    const wager = reach.formatCurrency(wagerAtomic, 4);\n    return await new Promise(resolveAcceptedP => {\n      this.setState({view: 'AcceptTerms', wager, resolveAcceptedP});\n    });\n  }\n  termsAccepted() {\n    this.state.resolveAcceptedP();\n    this.setState({view: 'WaitingForTurn'});\n  }\n  render() { return renderView(this, AttacherViews); }\n}\n\nrenderDOM(<App />);\" href=\"#\"></a></div><ol class=\"snippet\"><li value=\"1\"><a href=\"https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Statements/import\" id=\"p_456\" class=\"pid\"></i>We wrote about a hundred lines of Reach and two different frontends.\n  Our command-line version is about a hundred lines of JavaScript, while our Web version is about the same length, but has a lot of presentation code as well.<a href=\"#p_456\" class=\"pid\">456</a>\n</p>\n<p>\n  <i id=\"p_457\" class=\"pid\"></i>Behind the scenes, Reach generated hundreds of lines of Solidity (which you can look at here: <a href=\"https://github.com/reach-sh/reach-lang/tree/master/examples/rps-8-interact/build/index.main.sol\"><code>rps-8-interact/build/index.main.sol</code></a>), almost two thousand lines of TEAL (which you can look at here: <a href=\"https://github.com/reach-sh/reach-lang/tree/master/examples/rps-8-interact/build/index.main.appApproval.teal\"><code>rps-8-interact/build/index.main.appApproval.teal</code></a>), as well as over a thousand lines of JavaScript (which you can look at here: <a href=\"https://github.com/reach-sh/reach-lang/tree/master/examples/rps-8-interact/build/index.main.mjs\"><code>rps-8-interact/build/index.main.mjs</code></a>).\n  If we weren't using Reach, then we'd have to write all this code ourselves and ensure that they are consistent and updated at every change to the application.<a href=\"#p_457\" class=\"pid\">457</a>\n</p>\n<p><i id=\"p_458\" class=\"pid\"></i>Now that you've seen an entire Reach application from beginning to end, it's time for you to start working on your own applications!<a href=\"#p_458\" class=\"pid\">458</a></p>\n<ul>\n  <li><i id=\"p_459\" class=\"pid\"></i>You may want to start <a href=\"/workshop/#workshop\">the workshop</a>, which is a self-study course on practicing and learning Reach through different specific projects.<a href=\"#p_459\" class=\"pid\">459</a></li>\n  <li><i id=\"p_460\" class=\"pid\"></i>Or, maybe you'd like to spend some time in <a href=\"/guide/#guide\">the guide</a> learning about the background of some of the concepts used in Reach programs.<a href=\"#p_460\" class=\"pid\">460</a></li>\n  <li><i id=\"p_461\" class=\"pid\"></i>Or, maybe it's time for you to dive into <a href=\"/tool/#ref\">the reference</a> and look into the minutiae of Reach's features.<a href=\"#p_461\" class=\"pid\">461</a></li>\n  <li><i id=\"p_462\" class=\"pid\"></i>Finally, you may like to repeat a portion of this tutorial, but using <a href=\"/tut/rps/7-rpc/#tut-7-rpc\">a language other than JavaScript</a>, like Python or Go!<a href=\"#p_462\" class=\"pid\">462</a></li>\n</ul>\n<p>\n  <i id=\"p_463\" class=\"pid\"></i>No matter what you decide to read or work on next, we hope you'll join us on <a
